21.03.19 15:34:00<editable-dog>hey i gotta run again for a hour or so
21.03.19 15:38:15<stoopkid_> so i guess it depends on how you personally conceive of this as a parameter, i.e. if it's something that should be individually modifiable per-link or is just a global fix for making links work properly and that it shouldn't ever be disabled
21.03.19 15:39:16<stoopkid_> but this is maybe a good example of what i mean, we don't want to express this in terms of "their" logic, we want it to be expressed in terms of our logic
21.03.19 15:40:26<stoopkid_> so the "fix" isn't the feature, the feature is whether or not same-page hrefs will jump back to where they're supposed to if you click them twice
21.03.19 15:41:12<stoopkid_> if this should be a user-customizable feature, the default should probably be true and apply globally to all links, i'd say
21.03.19 15:41:30<stoopkid_> then how we manifest that configuration into reality is something we should handle elsewhere
21.03.19 15:47:14<stoopkid_> so wrt big picture wrt layout, data integration, etc.. let's say you have a "blog-post" feature on your site
21.03.19 15:47:53<stoopkid_> in HTML/CSS whatever that might be a thousand lines of layout template and styling options
21.03.19 15:48:45<stoopkid_> but we probably have way fewer user-configurable parameters
21.03.19 15:50:36<stoopkid_> whatever is that schema of user-configurable parameters, we should have an actual schema corresponding to it, like a set of json fields associated w/ human readable names
21.03.19 15:51:39<stoopkid_> wrt that schema, it's composed of.. say.. a header, a subheading w/ date & author, and then an "article"
21.03.19 15:52:30<stoopkid_> each of these things should be editable
21.03.19 15:53:55<stoopkid_> like wysiwyg you click on the header and it transforms into a textbox letting you input the heading text, select font stylings etc..
21.03.19 15:54:18<stoopkid_> and etc.. for each of the other components
21.03.19 15:55:58<stoopkid_> wrt to the layout of "blog-post", we should be able to express it just a single time
21.03.19 15:56:25<stoopkid_> just the equivalent of <header/> <subheading/> <article/>
21.03.19 15:57:49<stoopkid_> and this should automatically account for the wysiwyg editing of "blog-post" unless we have something specific to the layout of blog-posts beyond whatever already comes packaged with the editing for header/subheading/article
21.03.19 16:01:45<stoopkid_> so that's basically the idea, you have component A, which comes in A-static and A-editable forms, then you make component B which just simply includes A, and B should automatically be wysiwyg editable by giving you access to A's editable version
21.03.19 16:06:35<stoopkid_> so then this basically corresponds to some json object:
21.03.19 16:09:31<stoopkid_> B { name-of-A-object: A; ...other values specific to B...}
21.03.19 16:10:58<stoopkid_> this is like a schema for B so let's say A included header/subheading/article its schema object would be:
21.03.19 16:11:37<stoopkid_> A { header-for-A: Header; subheading-for-A: Subheading; article-for-A: Article }
21.03.19 16:13:36<stoopkid_> so now you can have objects like my-obj-A { header-for-A: ..header value... ; subheading-for-A: ...subheading value...; article-for-A: ... article value ... }
21.03.19 16:18:02<stoopkid_> so let's say B was Site and A was Blog-Post
21.03.19 16:19:30<stoopkid_> when you wysiwyg edit Blog-Post you'll just be making edits to a json object my-site.my-blog-post
21.03.19 16:20:12<stoopkid_> or rather, that will be the result of wysiwyg editing
21.03.19 16:38:27<stoopkid_> so basically each human-level component should have all of the following (or equivalents of them) bundled together: a vue template for its static version, a vue template for its editable version, a json schema representing the user-configurable options for the component, and the js code that the server can use to expose the methods that handle responding to the wysiwyg interaction (both browser & server-side)
21.03.19 16:44:53<stoopkid_> wrt the editable vs. static versions of content, it should basically be like they're just two different stylings of the same DOM
21.03.19 16:45:04<stoopkid_> not precisely, but the same analogy
21.03.19 16:46:04<stoopkid_> so any layout that includes component A should be able to work with both the static layout and the editable layout for A
21.03.19 16:47:05<stoopkid_> so if B includes A, we don't need to make a separate editable B that includes editable A, B should just say it includes A, and then be able to work with both the static and editable versions of A without any further modification
21.03.19 16:49:33<stoopkid_> you *can* then add an editable version of B for editing things specific to B, and the editable layout for B should also be able to just say it includes A, and accommodate both the static and editable versions without any further modification
21.03.19 16:51:35<stoopkid_> and further it should just already be equipped to talk to the server to send its modifications, without any further configuration
21.03.19 16:52:30<stoopkid_> so basically you should just be able to write:
21.03.19 16:52:43<stoopkid_> <template>
21.03.19 16:52:50<stoopkid_>  <Header>
21.03.19 16:52:56<stoopkid_> <Subheading>
21.03.19 16:52:58<stoopkid_> <Article>
21.03.19 16:53:01<stoopkid_> </template>
21.03.19 16:54:33<stoopkid_> and automatically get a site that's already wysiwyg editable by exposing whatever whatever wysiwyg editing functionality is already available in each of <Header> <Subheading> and <Article>

22.03.19 08:53:13<stoopkid__> so here's the issue i'm currently having wrt wrestling html/css down to something sane
22.03.19 08:54:18<stoopkid__> say you want a div to expand vertically to fit its content, i.e. it expands instead of overflows
22.03.19 08:54:55<stoopkid__> it will actually automatically do that
22.03.19 08:55:11<stoopkid__> now let's say the content has content
22.03.19 08:55:38<stoopkid__> so div A contains div B which contains div C
22.03.19 08:55:54<stoopkid__> let's say div C overflows B, this won't be accounted for by A
22.03.19 08:56:52<stoopkid__> so A will expand to accommodate its child elements, ex. B, but it won't expand to accommodate its grandchild elements, ex. C and later descendants
22.03.19 09:09:04<stoopkid__> in general things shouldn't overflow their containers but there might be some situations where it's called for and as we've seen it's something that can happen by accident so our layouts should be designed to be as accommodating as possible
22.03.19 09:10:44<stoopkid__> in that regard i'm thinking that in general the right side of the page should be left empty just in case some text content is not formatted properly and overflows to the right
22.03.19 09:13:02<stoopkid__> and with this thing w/ the divs not expanding to the size of their grandchild divs, if there's a fix for that it should be applied on essentially every single div that doesn't intentionally have some overflow as part of the design
22.03.19 09:32:29<editable-dog>whats the css attribute that enables the stretch-to-child behavior?
22.03.19 09:35:57<stoopkid__> (most) divs automatically stretch/shrink vertically to fit children and stretch/shrink horizontally to fill parent, unless other settings are applied
22.03.19 09:36:35<editable-dog>hmm
22.03.19 09:38:05<editable-dog>so how are you making them stretch horizontally to contain children?
22.03.19 09:49:40<stoopkid__> display: flex on the parent seems to work for some examples, although it can have side-effects
22.03.19 09:52:25<editable-dog>any other methods? or do we just apply this attribute to every div and its done?
